  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7f12a683-c513-4a91-9fe2-6905edf25c5a'
      });
    }

<div id="review_156549471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156549471" />
    <a title="Sailesh Ravindran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4943980-sailesh-ravindran"><img alt="Sailesh Ravindran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441855866p2/4943980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156549471?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sailesh Ravindran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sailesh Ravindran" href="/user/show/4943980-sailesh-ravindran">Sailesh Ravindran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156549471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5272651980917339151">Once again, some great reviews is what led me to reading this book. The book, they say, is a true love tale, written by Ravinder out of the despair of losing his girlfriend. But, the writing is irritatingly immature. Considering it a true account, this could have been excused if only it had been written with some confidence. He goes on repeating the phrase '...because i am madly in love with Khushi' over and over again, as if he thinks that a reader might actually not understand it. Another irri</span>
  <span id="freeText5272651980917339151" style="display:none">Once again, some great reviews is what led me to reading this book. The book, they say, is a true love tale, written by Ravinder out of the despair of losing his girlfriend. But, the writing is irritatingly immature. Considering it a true account, this could have been excused if only it had been written with some confidence. He goes on repeating the phrase '...because i am madly in love with Khushi' over and over again, as if he thinks that a reader might actually not understand it. Another irritating thing that the writer does is to always quote Khushi as 'Khushi- the one i love'. Oh! Come on, aren't we reading the lovestory of Ravinder and Khushi.<br /><br />I would also say that this guy has been bitten by the 'Chetan Bhagt bug' a little too severely. The writer has written the book with an eye on the Bollywood. The characters in the story are just too ideal and perfect that you can actually spot them in any Yash Raj Movie. <br /><br />But yes, if you have enjoyed all those Yash Raj Movies, if you are looking for a light read, if you are travelling and have lot of time to spare but not money, and if you really don't care about what your co-passengers might assume about your reading habits, well, then this book is a very good option.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5272651980917339151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_374317754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/374317754" />
    <a title="Dona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10681424-dona"><img alt="Dona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389284649p2/10681424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/374317754?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dona" href="/user/show/10681424-dona">Dona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10681424-dona?shelf=indian-english-authors">indian-english-authors</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer374317754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer678948161334121907">D title says ‘I TOO HAD A LOVE STORY’ ( Did he really? I ‘m not very sure whether it was love or sum guy gloating over it..He checks out an air-hostess while his ’soulmate’ is dying & has d audacity 2 paint himself innocent..u call dis luv??)<br/><br/>Guess vat, it is a stupid, stupid book! Riding on d Chetan Bhagat bandwagon, here cums anoder Indian writer wid a so called’ heartbreaking true love tale’. Its d story of Ravin, who falls in luv wid a girl whom he met on a matrimonial site n finally loses he</span>
  <span id="freeText678948161334121907" style="display:none">D title says ‘I TOO HAD A LOVE STORY’ ( Did he really? I ‘m not very sure whether it was love or sum guy gloating over it..He checks out an air-hostess while his ’soulmate’ is dying &amp; has d audacity 2 paint himself innocent..u call dis luv??)<br /><br />Guess vat, it is a stupid, stupid book! Riding on d Chetan Bhagat bandwagon, here cums anoder Indian writer wid a so called’ heartbreaking true love tale’. Its d story of Ravin, who falls in luv wid a girl whom he met on a matrimonial site n finally loses her 2 fate.The style of writing is very much similar 2 dat of Bhagats, but a lot worse. Its filled wid cheesy dialogues n attempts at jokes at even d deathbed. My collagemates who had read it described it as humourous, among many oder things. If dis is ur definition of humour, den mind u, I am not d person 2 b wid. While I was reading d buk, I was not sure whether I really hated it or was it an ok-ok type. Den came appoint ver I read :<br />“ V r trying our best , but der is no guarantee dat, 4 d rest of her life,she vil b as beautiful as she was b4. Thank u 4 standing by her.” ( D entire conversation lasts almost a page) Dat was d final blow 4 me.It was really easy 2 hate d buk after dat.<br /><br />If dis is his real life luv story &amp; d fact dat he dedicated almost a page 2 how a nurse tells him how gud a person he is, den dat tells a lot about d author. R good men so scarce on earth dat v label any guy as good?( By good ‘men’, I don’t mean humanity as such, only d men(u knw, d 1 wid d XY chromosome) coz der r enough good women in d world hidden behind veils imposed by d society n d 4 walls of a kitchen imposed by family. If all der goodness ver 2 b radiated, devil wud probably go blind!)<br /><br />Oh, &amp; he tries 2 show his respect 4 women too( anoder failed attempt 2 boast himself). <br /><br />In d buk ’ d fountainhead’, Elsworth says dat a gud critic shud b 1 who shud b able 2 impose his ideas on d society.. If he labels a bad buk as excellent, den it shud bcum d bestseller.. I can only understand d success of dis buk as d outome of sumthing sinister like dat. If dis makes a nation cry, den mayb v r a nation looking 4 reasons 2 cry. If dis is true luv, den mayb v r too blinded by bollywood romances.<br /><br />In Atlas Shrugged, Rand says “All that is necessary for the triumph of evil is that good men do nothing.” (U guessed it rit, I luv Ayn Rand!).. All dat is necessary 4 d success of a bad buk is d scarcity of honest reviews. Der is a lot of positive opinion about d buk dat d negativity drowns in it. Hence, dis review.<br /><br />D succcess of dis book reminds me of a conversation between d American President &amp; his aide Lewis in d movie 'D American President':<br />Lewis : " People don't have a choice! Bob Rumson is the only one doing the talking! People want leadership, Mr. President, and in the absence of genuine leadership, they'll listen to anyone who steps up to the microphone. They want leadership. They're so thirsty for it they'll crawl through the desert toward a mirage, and when they discover there's no water, they'll drink the sand."<br /> <br />President : "Lewis, we've had presidents who were beloved, who couldn't find a coherent sentence with two hands and a flashlight. People don't drink the sand because they're thirsty. They drink the sand because they don't know the difference."<br /><br />D same applies in d case of books. People make bestsellers out of nonsense due 2 d absence of gud books. I can only hope dat sumbody sumwhere mit b toiling on a brilliant manuscript now 2 save us frm buks like des.<br /><br />In short, I hate d book. I hate d book so much dat i managed 2 drag my lazy ass out of bed n write dis. Read d book, so dat u know ver ur standards r. D cover of d book says ‘National Bestseller’. If dis is d kind of book dat bcums a national bestseller, den I shud assume d whole nation has gone nuts!</span>

<div id="review_592589468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592589468" />
    <a title="Hershey " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19468761-hershey"><img alt="Hershey " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599546236p2/19468761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592589468?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hershey " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hershey " href="/user/show/19468761-hershey">Hershey </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592589468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14652688810149268881"><b> Awfully written novel which killed the story. </b> <br/><br/>This book was suggested to me by my dear friend who loved this book. I normally avoid tragic - romance books. But the way my friend described it made me want to give it a try. <br/><br/>Here's what happened.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417955i/827198.jpg' alt=' photo catsleepingonabook_zps131dae5d.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>Sleep was inevitable. But I somehow managed to read the book, to read the pages that lacked savor. It was a bitter boring read. It was like biting an apple that was about to rot. <br/><br/>The story is about the author, Ravi who meets a girl in an internet dating </span>
  <span id="freeText14652688810149268881" style="display:none"><b> Awfully written novel which killed the story. </b> <br><br>This book was suggested to me by my dear friend who loved this book. I normally avoid tragic - romance books. But the way my friend described it made me want to give it a try. <br><br>Here's what happened.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417955i/827198.jpg" alt=" photo catsleepingonabook_zps131dae5d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Sleep was inevitable. But I somehow managed to read the book, to read the pages that lacked savor. It was a bitter boring read. It was like biting an apple that was about to rot. <br><br>The story is about the author, Ravi who meets a girl in an internet dating website and falls in love with her. That's it. The rest of the story goes very slow - paced. It's all about Kushi and Ravi. There's nothing else to lean on when those two characters get boring which (believe me) they did. The story would have been better if there were many events happening simultaneously or if the author didn't concentrate only about his love life. <br><br>The author wasn't very descriptive; for example he stated that "the food was tasty". He never mentioned what food he was referring to. He could have substituted the word 'tasty' to some other more descriptive word; for example scrumptious. Or at least he could have mentioned what he was eating. And that particular phrase remained with me long enough for me to write it in this review. It was a long time ago since I read this book and I'm surprised that the first phrase that came to my mind was "the food was tasty".<br><br>The author's narrative skills were very poor and that is why sleep was inevitable. Maybe a better usage of vocabulary would have gained this book another star.<br><br>The story was cute on the whole but the writing killed it. If you love the story and not the words that describe it then, this book would be perfect. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14652688810149268881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Archit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54103953-archit"><img alt="Archit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526805090p2/54103953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1588204339?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Archit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Archit" href="/user/show/54103953-archit">Archit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54103953-archit?shelf=books-we-own">books-we-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1588204339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9855106767335923123">I will give this one a five star without being generous. These light-hearted reads had been in the trend in the book sales. <br/><br/>And I picked on up before a tiresome overnight journey.<br/><br/>The story is indeed good and I will reserve my rating explanation for just the ending. It had me captured and had my attention!<br/><br/>Brisking and trotting the tale at his will, Ravinder Singh did a good sound job throwing the ending in the face - <i>right out of the blue</i>.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“She died. I survived. Because I survived, I die everyd</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText9855106767335923123" style="display:none">I will give this one a five star without being generous. These light-hearted reads had been in the trend in the book sales. <br /><br />And I picked on up before a tiresome overnight journey.<br /><br />The story is indeed good and I will reserve my rating explanation for just the ending. It had me captured and had my attention!<br /><br />Brisking and trotting the tale at his will, Ravinder Singh did a good sound job throwing the ending in the face - <i>right out of the blue</i>.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“She died. I survived. Because I survived, I die everyday.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The events are carved out in a seasoned manner and the writing style is best described as nifty. There is a strange, detached, numbness that I find hard to fathom.<br /><br /><blockquote><i>“Tere jaane ka asar kuch aisa hua mujh par, tujhe dhoondate dhoondate, maine khud ko paa liya”</i><br />- a line I stumbled upon in the pages</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <i>5 Stars</i>
</b> for the way this book made me feel.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Simple yet moving.</b>
</i></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer399905610&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer399905610" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5260990326243879876">i read this book a year back or so. a few of my friends actually cried reading this( all of them who did being girls), so i was forced and yeah also out of curiosity i decided to read this book. let me summarise what i understood from this book for you.<br/><br/>there's this indian techie who falls in love with the girl who he meets on a matrimonial site and unfortunately she dies in an accident before their marriage. it being a true story, i feel sad for this guy. yes i truly do. <br/>ok thats all is the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText5260990326243879876" style="display:none">i read this book a year back or so. a few of my friends actually cried reading this( all of them who did being girls), so i was forced and yeah also out of curiosity i decided to read this book. let me summarise what i understood from this book for you.<br /><br />there's this indian techie who falls in love with the girl who he meets on a matrimonial site and unfortunately she dies in an accident before their marriage. it being a true story, i feel sad for this guy. yes i truly do. <br />ok thats all is the story.<br /><br />now, about the writing. one word- USELESS!!! you'll forget your basic english if you read this one! i dont even know how this guy actually even got it published!! beyond me!! and if its about the love, i couldnt feel any love that pulled me into the story of the book. just simple and stale! <br /><br />moral: crappy book, don't waste your precious time on this. there're are better books by other indian author's and i dont mean chetan bhagat here. something more like Amitav Ghosh! :)<br /></span>

<div id="review_397930983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/397930983" />
    <a title="Mohit Parikh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5283792-mohit-parikh"><img alt="Mohit Parikh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481180988p2/5283792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/397930983?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohit Parikh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohit Parikh" href="/user/show/5283792-mohit-parikh">Mohit Parikh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5283792-mohit-parikh?shelf=india">india</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer397930983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7894833923301895764">My mother's fifteen year old student handed me this book, wanting me to read it, read it and love it as much as he did. When he persisted for a week, I finally decided to give it a go this night. <br/>It takes barely a page to understand that it is an uncomplicated and honest story, with easy to relate one dimensional Indian characters. English is bad, editing is worse, but the fact that the author wants to narrate the story 'as is', makes you leave aside all judgement and by the time the book ends, </span>
  <span id="freeText7894833923301895764" style="display:none">My mother's fifteen year old student handed me this book, wanting me to read it, read it and love it as much as he did. When he persisted for a week, I finally decided to give it a go this night. <br />It takes barely a page to understand that it is an uncomplicated and honest story, with easy to relate one dimensional Indian characters. English is bad, editing is worse, but the fact that the author wants to narrate the story 'as is', makes you leave aside all judgement and by the time the book ends, you are but touched. The mystical experience near the end of the book even gave me goosebumps. <br /><br />But judging this book as a work of fiction and not autobiographical, I will grade it as extremely poor. The narrator displays an astounding lack of self-awareness. Neither his observations display any acuity (most revolving around the cheerful childishness of a girl) nor his commentaries possess any psychological depth (froth with banal generalities like [paraphrasing] "it is human tendency to hate the person who gets you up in the morning then thank him", or, "we think we are smart because we are young; but we forget our parents are elder, so they must be smarter than us"). Prose is repetitive and burdened with unnecessary details. Not all phone calls should start with a 'Hiiiiiiii' and a 'Heyyy!'. Not all hotel names and street names and room numbers and car-makes and relations have to be mentioned. A girl can be more than 'beautiful' and readers know all-too-well how much you love her, they do not need reminding twice every page. <br /><br />All in all, the author is the *very* typical, unoriginal nice-guy-next-door. He experiences the most significant incident in his life - the coming and going of a girl - and he decides to share this experience with others in all its earnestness. I respect him for that. <br /><br />P.S. The innocence and motivation behind the book reminds me of another such work, 'Anything for you, Ma'am'. Back in 2006, I had chased down its author, Tushar Raheja, after several desperate emails. I wanted to get some tips on creative writing, some inside information on publishing industry and the magical formula, if any, for success. He was nice enough to share it. "Art comes from the heart," he had proffered. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7894833923301895764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aditi Sinai carapurcar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aditi Sinai carapurcar" href="/user/show/19373719-aditi-sinai-carapurcar">Aditi Sinai carapurcar</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589417259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10831439452961650388">I fail to understand how a guy can fall in love with a girl whom he hasnt even met. The even more surprising fact is that the family of both the main characters seem cool with it. The repetitive use of shona, love you, and continuous conversations seem more like addiction than love. The part where he continues talking even during take-off is nothing more than childish. <br/><br/>The author has made references where he has met the girls family personally while there is not a single instance where the guy's</span>
  <span id="freeText10831439452961650388" style="display:none">I fail to understand how a guy can fall in love with a girl whom he hasnt even met. The even more surprising fact is that the family of both the main characters seem cool with it. The repetitive use of shona, love you, and continuous conversations seem more like addiction than love. The part where he continues talking even during take-off is nothing more than childish. <br /><br />The author has made references where he has met the girls family personally while there is not a single instance where the guy's family has even seen the girl. Hence it is hard to believe that such parents exist in our society that go ahead with their son's engagement without seeing the girl.<br /><br />This book deserves nothing more than 2 stars. The book lacks interest. There is nothing which might keep the reader hooked. There is too much description of unnecessary things and unwanted characters. <br /><br />Author has dedicated an entire chapter in the beginning of the book to his best friends but they are not mentioned even once in the end of the book when I suppose they were needed the most after khushi's death. <br /><br />Book is full of immature love. Perhaps the title should have been " I too had a fairy tale".</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_144443968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144443968" />
    <a title="Meenakshi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3423072-meenakshi"><img alt="Meenakshi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325270384p2/3423072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144443968?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meenakshi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meenakshi" href="/user/show/3423072-meenakshi">Meenakshi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144443968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9229928395365980844">Love stories with a tragic end are beautiful in their own peculair way.Some love stories never die. They remain for generations yet to come to read them again...this is one such story....<br/>Though I am not the kind who'd read romantic novels on a lazy Sunday morning just to pass time but I knew this one had something special about it even before I started reading it.<br/>Boy was the story touching!!..? To know it is a true story was even more touching and I could feel the pain the author must have gone </span>
  <span id="freeText9229928395365980844" style="display:none">Love stories with a tragic end are beautiful in their own peculair way.Some love stories never die. They remain for generations yet to come to read them again...this is one such story....<br />Though I am not the kind who'd read romantic novels on a lazy Sunday morning just to pass time but I knew this one had something special about it even before I started reading it.<br />Boy was the story touching!!..? To know it is a true story was even more touching and I could feel the pain the author must have gone through, through his words. The pace and pitch of the story made for an extremely enjoyable read as I could relate to the emotions that spilled out of the writer’s heart into the pages of the book.I could easily identify with the descriptions of late night conversations, quarrels, the fear of facing parents and little tears and smiles, related with light hearted humor and child like simplicity.This is a must read for all those who value emotions &amp; feelings. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9229928395365980844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

To know its a true story was even more touching and I co</span>
  <span id="freeText16327425523662225535" style="display:none">Some books take you for a surprise. I was recently browsing a bookshop and came across a lot of young aspiring Indian Authors. Most of them were chicklits and female authors but to find a male author in this selection was a surprise. The title of the book struck a chord with me. Even I too had a love story....so I picked the book. Haven't never heard about the author nor the book. I felt I should try reading it, and boy did I feel touched. To know its a true story was even more touching and I could feel the pain the author must have gone through, through his words. It had a similar effect as Erich Segal's Love Story did to me. I would recommend this book to one and all.<br /><br />P.S. Please don't make a trashy Hindi movie of this book adaptation. If you guys can't do justification don't ever make a movie.<br /><br />Synopsis<br />Do love stories ever die?<br />Can modern day gadgets like mobile phones and the ‘http:\\ www’ era of internet bring you the love of your life?<br />You haven’t met her earlier, but commit to marry. Will you still call this a love marriage?<br />And what if on the engagement day while you pull the ring out from your pocket, you realize what you planned was just a dream which never comes true…?<br />How would you react when a beautiful person comes into your life, becomes your most precious possession and then one day goes away from you…forever?<br />Not all love stories are meant to have a perfect ending. Some stay incomplete. Yet they are beautiful in their own way. Ravin’s love story is one such innocent and beautiful story. He believes love stories seldom die. They are meant to stay for the generations yet to come and read them. And given that one chance to narrate his love story, this is how he began…<br />…I remember the date well: 4th March 2006. I was in Kolkata and about to reach Happy’s home. I had been very excited all morning as I was going to see our gang of four after three years.<br /><br />About the Author<br />Ravinder Singh (26 years) is a software engineer who works with a prominent IT company in India.He was brought up in a very small town of Orissa called Burla. After spending most of his life there,he has recently moved to Chandigarh. Owing to the nature of his work, he has visited various parts of<br />the world and he wishes to continue doing the same in future. Apart from reading and writing, the author has a keen interest in working out in the gym.<br />Occasionally, he loves playing snooker; his favorite game. He is crazy about Punjabi music and loves dancing to its beats. ‘I too had a love story’ is his<br />debut novel. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_605197044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Priyanka Roy Banerjee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Priyanka Roy Banerjee" href="/user/show/16960674-priyanka-roy-banerjee">Priyanka Roy Banerjee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16960674-priyanka-roy-banerjee?shelf=indian-authors">indian-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer605197044&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605197044" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6488333852865662046">I had seen glimpses of this book here and there on various websites, but did not have the time or reason to give it a read. Recently a friend mentioned that the author is her friend’s relative and its a true story. So I grabbed a copy hoping it would be worth, but..I surely was disappointed. The plot is touching indeed, there is no doubt about that. Who wouldn’t want to read a love story about a couple who meet and part by death? The kernel of the story is pretty appealing with attributes like a</span>
  <span id="freeText6488333852865662046" style="display:none">I had seen glimpses of this book here and there on various websites, but did not have the time or reason to give it a read. Recently a friend mentioned that the author is her friend’s relative and its a true story. So I grabbed a copy hoping it would be worth, but..I surely was disappointed. The plot is touching indeed, there is no doubt about that. Who wouldn’t want to read a love story about a couple who meet and part by death? The kernel of the story is pretty appealing with attributes like a foreword written by N.R. Narayana Murthy (ex-CEO and co-founder of Infosys) and the author being an MBA from a leading B-school in India. All these attract the readers, especially the teenage ones looking for some extra mush in their hectic lives. But, and there is a big BUT here, the writing style did not attract me at all. I confess I’m not a big fan of the recent ‘Indianized’ style of writing which most authors nowadays attempt to. Ravinder Singh is no exception as he writes lucidly in ‘Indian English’ with quite a lot of Hindi words interspersed. While his writing has earned him fans worldwide, I failed to find a single sentence written so beautifully that it would leave an imprint on my mind. The author has tried to explore very light eroticism in the romantic spots of the story, but it is so restrained that it doesn’t really make any sense to me.<br /><br />I doubt if I have the credentials to judge an author so critically, but as a reader I expected better ways of expressing the content since the plot did not have any element of suspense or thrill. I did not like reading whole sentences and conversations in Hindi where the is novel supposedly written in English. I have no idea how the sequel would turn out to be, nonetheless, I’ll keep an eye on it too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6488333852865662046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_584753616" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/584753616" />
    <a title="Bibek Thapa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7193378-bibek-thapa"><img alt="Bibek Thapa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578574685p2/7193378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/584753616?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibek Thapa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibek Thapa" href="/user/show/7193378-bibek-thapa">Bibek Thapa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19308015-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7193378-bibek-thapa?shelf=full-length-novels">full-length-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7193378-bibek-thapa?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584753616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9132318131792449982">*Disclaimer: This review contains spoilers and some strong language. So be warned*<br/><br/>I Too Had a Love Story is one of the most over-hyper piece of crap I've ever read.<br/>Supposedly, this is a true story of the author, Ravin, and the girl "whom [he] loved, yet couldn't marry", Kushi. Even if this story was complete fiction, I don't think I would have wanted Kushi to end up with Ravin. Ever.<br/><br/>I haven't read a lot of Indian authors, but the one's I have read have a good grasp of the English language. Sadly</span>
  <span id="freeText9132318131792449982" style="display:none">*Disclaimer: This review contains spoilers and some strong language. So be warned*<br /><br />I Too Had a Love Story is one of the most over-hyper piece of crap I've ever read.<br />Supposedly, this is a true story of the author, Ravin, and the girl "whom [he] loved, yet couldn't marry", Kushi. Even if this story was complete fiction, I don't think I would have wanted Kushi to end up with Ravin. Ever.<br /><br />I haven't read a lot of Indian authors, but the one's I have read have a good grasp of the English language. Sadly, that wasn't the case here. The language and descriptions felt juvenile and kept bringing down the story. I wasn't expecting the story and the words to sweep me off my feet but what I got was immensely worse.<br /> <pre>
  <i>I oxygenated my lungs with a deep breath and turned her almost 180 degrees </i>
</pre><br />What's wrong with good old, I took in a deep breath?<br /><br />One of the biggest problems that I had with this story was Ravin. He was so self-righteous and vain that this story didn't feel like his and Kushi's tragic love story but more of an affirmation of what a "good" guy he is. Which btw he is not. He see flaws in everyone but rarely in himself.<br />When he first joins Shaadi.com this is what he writes:<br /> <br /><pre>
  <i>The best ones had declined me. In fact, most of them had ignored me. Only a handful accepted my request but, unfortunately, they didn't appear that good. </i>
</pre><br /><br />And than later, just before he is supposed to meet Kushi face-to-face for the first time:<br /><br /><pre>
  <i>What if she isn't as beautiful as she appears in her pictures? What if she laughs n a very weird way? What if she limps?</i>
</pre><br /><br />Notice how he only talks about the shortcoming or the fear of shortcomings on others. There isn't a single line there where he thinks <i>What if Kushi finds</i> me <i>lacking?</i> <br /><br />Also, his self-flagellation doesn't end there. What could have been a moment of genuine social criticism on misogyny and male entitlement, turned into yet another moment of making himself the knight in shinning armor:<br /><br /><pre>
  <i>The city was not safe for women, especially at night, when the savages of the city came out of their dens and did all manner of ill. So, maybe, her mother felt some comfort knowing I was with Kushi. </i>
</pre><br /><br />And this moment comes after this one:<br /><br /><pre>
  <i>'Men build houses, but women make homes.' And now I had found one such woman.</i>
</pre><br /><br />Let me tell you of yet another moment of epic assholery. So our dude Ravin is late getting to the airport and even there he doesn't pay much attention to the announcement. So when Kushi tells him that the announcement may be for him, he asks an American guy next to him <i>"Wudgyaa mind tellin me whom they were calling for?"</i> to which the American guy replied, justifiable, <i>Some Ravin to New York. For fuck's sake, why are people not on time at the airport?"</i><br /><br />Now our dude Ravin, does say that while he was angry at the guy, he didn't say anything because it was his fault. If the interaction had ended here it would have been fine. But when he goes to the check-in counter and finds out that he's been upgraded to business class, this is what he does:<br /><br /><pre>
  <i>While talking to her I saw the same passenger passing by - the one with the US flag on his T-shirt. I waved at him sarcastically and he moved ahead to economy class as if he hadn't seen me. But I knew he had. </i>
</pre><br /><br />Could you be any more mean-spirited and petty for something that was your fault to begin with?<br /><br />Now, for the crème de la crème of the whole thing. As you maybe have guessed given the title. This love story is that of the Nicholas Sparks variety, i.e. one of them dies at the end. <br /><br />So after a fatal accident, Kushi is in the ICU and Ravin in on the way to see her. Now, I understand that we all have different coping mechanism when it comes to tragic events. Not everyone reacts and deals with them the same way. Having said that, how do you start flirting with the air hostess when you are on you way to see your possibly-dying love of your life?<br /><br /><pre>
  <i> Even her lovely face could not get me to say yes. Maybe because no one appeared as beautiful to me, anymore, as my own Kushi...<br /><br />...'Ok. Veg or non-veg, sir?; she smiled.<br />Wow! This time that smile appeared good to me. <br />'You won't be serving me both?' I asked her as soon as she completed her question...<br /><br />...'Wow! That smile is pretty indeed,' I told myself. </i>
</pre><br /><br />This book was honestly really bad. I went into it because i had seen so many people raving about it. The book itself has rave reviews printed on it from some of the big newspapers and magazines in India. So, I not only feel bad, I feel cheated. If there is anything that I can say to the author, it's this: show, don't tell.<br /><br />Read this book at your own risk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9132318131792449982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer507944116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer356916576088125270">first of all, lets not compare Indian authors with the western authors. keeping that in mind, the book is gud and touching. sadly the narration is not up to the mark. you can sympathise with the author but it doesnt go beyond that. there are a few places where the tale gets mushy and u cant help but roll ur eyes. also the comments in the brackets make the book look more like a personal diary than a bestseller. the forced humour is also a turn off at a few places.<br/>while reading it, almost every pe</span>
  <span id="freeText356916576088125270" style="display:none">first of all, lets not compare Indian authors with the western authors. keeping that in mind, the book is gud and touching. sadly the narration is not up to the mark. you can sympathise with the author but it doesnt go beyond that. there are a few places where the tale gets mushy and u cant help but roll ur eyes. also the comments in the brackets make the book look more like a personal diary than a bestseller. the forced humour is also a turn off at a few places.<br />while reading it, almost every person who has been/is in love will relate to the book, cry over it and the book will find a place in their heart. but thats the emotional side of us doing all this. if u sit down and think rationally, a few evident loop holes will definitely surface.<br />i am not here to criticise Indian authors bcoz its not going to fetch me a prize. in my opinion, it is a gud thing the author shared his story with us but it wasnt that exciting. there is plenty of room for improvement.<br />the "die hard romantic" side of me enjoyed the book but the "serious reader" side was disappointed. so if ur heart rules ur head, go read the book but if your head rules your heart, please grab a copy of a sci-fi book instead.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204516574" />
    <a title="Jyoti Babel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5262696-jyoti-babel"><img alt="Jyoti Babel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388421593p2/5262696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204516574?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jyoti Babel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jyoti Babel" href="/user/show/5262696-jyoti-babel">Jyoti Babel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204516574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11078659610290543808">The author tells his love story through this book. It has a tragic end, which explains the past tense of the title. It is the love story of Ravin and Khushi. The author tells how he met the girl of her dreams and how their love bloomed. But, things doesn't happen as he had thought as destiny had other plans for them. Giving out more about the story would not do justice to any aspiring readers. So, read the book to find out more. Having said that,I must add that if you are looking for a literary </span>
  <span id="freeText11078659610290543808" style="display:none">The author tells his love story through this book. It has a tragic end, which explains the past tense of the title. It is the love story of Ravin and Khushi. The author tells how he met the girl of her dreams and how their love bloomed. But, things doesn't happen as he had thought as destiny had other plans for them. Giving out more about the story would not do justice to any aspiring readers. So, read the book to find out more. Having said that,I must add that if you are looking for a literary piece than it's not one. If you are looking for a meticulously crafted plot in the story, it doesn't have one. What catches your attention in this book, is the simplicity of the book and the honesty with which the author has written it, and that this story is based on his own love story makes you empathize with the author for having gone through a difficult patch in life.<br /><br />The story is plainly written yet beautifully executed. All emotions conveyed through the story are delivered. It is indeed a touching love story and it did struck a chord in my heart.<br /><br />It is the kind of book I would prefer when I am in a mood for a light read.<br /><br />The author has put his heart and soul in writing this book.It will stay in your mind long after you have read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11078659610290543808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377679-shreeka?shelf=indian-authors">indian-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615278917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15577042189429682976">To be honest, I havent read books written by Indian authors. This was my first experience and really i didnt know what to expect. A friend of mine who loved this book lent it to me and i thought i could give it a try. I dont regret my decision because i actually liked this book. It was a simple love story with a tragic ending..well we all knew how the story was going to end like that since the title doesnt do much to hide that fact. And yes, I cried during the last moments.(what? im an emotional</span>
  <span id="freeText15577042189429682976" style="display:none">To be honest, I havent read books written by Indian authors. This was my first experience and really i didnt know what to expect. A friend of mine who loved this book lent it to me and i thought i could give it a try. I dont regret my decision because i actually liked this book. It was a simple love story with a tragic ending..well we all knew how the story was going to end like that since the title doesnt do much to hide that fact. And yes, I cried during the last moments.(what? im an emotional person!!) It could easily be recognised as one of those Bollywood stories... all it lacks is a bunch of songs in between!!lol!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15577042189429682976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_283645904" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283645904" />
    <a title="Santhosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7006637-santhosh"><img alt="Santhosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514875248p2/7006637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283645904?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Santhosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Santhosh" href="/user/show/7006637-santhosh">Santhosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788188575701" href="/book/show/19427193-i-too-had-a-love-story">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283645904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11226377780601864343">Though I appreciate the intent and emotions behind Ravinder's story and the amount of personal courage and desperate longing in writing this, I just can't forgive the bad writing from a obviously first-time writer. While the editors may have decided to let the book follow the natural flow of the author, there's a reason they have a job and a role in the industry.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MLUYcFcNP/wY7Q/W3V/PNj1kc5G0bhBiuJeFcqEA1f94+TcLA3eSsvlC/odWXsQ0x0hUNEPbo4SpTjU7p72oJw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8+IB+mBjmN5OlE3DPByUZx5xbxVz0E1YHLZ7fdGGu7S7ri6BNBk1kK87vJK3HZ9l5F1IsIRl/r4Nb8s01zvGbA==')})
  }

Press 2 for broken hearts.Press 3 if your life has totally crashed. . . . Six friends work nights at a call center in India, providing technical support for a major U.S. appliance corporation.   <span id="freeText8478943847293647578" style="display:none">Ravinder Singh is a software engineer who works with a prominent IT company in India.<br /><br />He was brought up in a very small town of Orissa called Burla. After spending most of his life there, he has recently moved to Chandigarh. Owing to the Nature of his work, he has visited various parts of the world and he wishes to continue doing the same in future. Apart from reading and writing, The Author has a keen interest in working out in the gym. Occasionally, he loves playing snooker; his favorite game. He is crazy about Punjabi Music and loves dancing to its beats. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7105461._I_Too_Had_A_Love_Story___" title=" I Too Had A Love Story.. " rel="nofollow noopener"> I Too Had A Love Story.. </a> is his debut novel.</span>
